If a log is truncated while it is being cleaned the cleaning of that log is aborted.\n    73→ * <p>\n    74→ * Messages with null payload are treated as deletes for the purpose of log compaction. This means that they receive special treatment by the cleaner.\n    75→ * The cleaner will only retain delete records for a period of time to avoid accumulating space indefinitely. This period of time is configurable on a per-topic\n    76→ * basis and is measured from the time the segment enters the clean portion of the log (at which point any prior message with that key has been removed).\n    77→ * Delete markers in the clean section of the log that are older than this time will not be retained when log segments are being recopied as part of cleaning.\n    78→ * This time is tracked by setting the base timestamp of a record batch with delete markers when the batch is recopied in the first cleaning that encounters\n    79→ * it. The relative timestamps of the records in the batch are also modified when recopied in this cleaning according to the new base timestamp of the batch.\n    80→ * <p>\n    81→ * Note that cleaning is more complicated with the idempotent/transactional producer capabilities. The following\n    82→ * are the key points:\n    83→ * <p>\n    84→ * <ol>\n    85→ * <li>In order to maintain sequence number continuity for active producers, we always retain the last batch\n    86→ *    from each producerId, even if all the records from the batch have been removed. The batch will be removed\n    87→ *    once the producer either writes a new batch or is expired due to inactivity.</li>\n    88→ * <li>We do not clean beyond the last stable offset. This ensures that all records observed by the cleaner have\n    89→ *    been decided (i.e. committed or aborted). In particular, this allows us to use the transaction index to\n    90→ *    collect the aborted transactions ahead of time.</li>\n    91→ * <li>Records from aborted transactions are removed by the cleaner immediately without regard to record keys.</li>\n    92→ * <li>Transaction markers are retained until all record batches from the same transaction have been removed and\n    93→ *    a sufficient amount of time has passed to reasonably ensure that an active consumer wouldn't consume any\n    94→ *    data from the transaction prior to reaching the offset of the marker. limitations under the License.\n */\npackage org.apache.kafka.storage.internals.log;\n\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.TopicPartition;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.config.AbstractConfig;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.config.ConfigException;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.errors.KafkaStorageException;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.utils.LogContext;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Time;\nimport org.apache.kafka.config.BrokerReconfigurable;\nimport org.apache.kafka.server.config.ServerConfigs;\nimport org.apache.kafka.server.metrics.KafkaMetricsGroup;\nimport org.apache.kafka.server.util.ShutdownableThread;\nimport org.apache.kafka.storage.internals.utils.Throttler;\n\nimport org.slf4j.Logger;\nimport org.slf4j.LoggerFactory;\n\nimport java.io.File;\nimport java.io.IOException;\nimport java.security.DigestException;\nimport java.security.NoSuchAlgorithmException;\nimport java.util.ArrayList;\nimport java.util.List;\nimport java.util.Map;\nimport java.util.Optional;\nimport java.util.Set;\nimport java.util.concurrent.ConcurrentMap;\nimport java.util.concurrent.TimeUnit;\nimport java.util.function.Function;\nimport java.util.stream.Collectors;\nimport java.util.stream.IntStream;\n\n/**\n * The cleaner is responsible for removing obsolete records from logs which have the \"compact\" retention strategy.\n * A message with key K and offset O is obsolete if there exists a message with key K and offset O' such that O < O'.\n * <p>\n * Each log can be thought of being split into two sections of segments: a \"clean\" section which has previously been cleaned followed by a\n * \"dirty\" section that has not yet been cleaned. The dirty section is further divided into the \"cleanable\" section followed by an \"uncleanable\" section.\n * The uncleanable section is excluded from cleaning. The active log segment is always uncleanable. If there is a\n * compaction lag time set, segments whose largest message timestamp is within the compaction lag time of the cleaning operation are also uncleanable.\n * <p>\n * The cleaning is carried out by a pool of background threads. Each thread chooses the dirtiest log that has the \"compact\" retention policy\n * and cleans that. The dirtiness of the log is guessed by taking the ratio of bytes in the dirty section of the log to the total bytes in the log.\n * <p>\n * To clean a log the cleaner first builds a mapping of key=>last_offset for the dirty section of the log. See {@link OffsetMap} for details of\n * the implementation of the mapping.\n * <p>\n * Once the key=>last_offset map is built, the log is cleaned by recopying each log segment but omitting any key that appears in the offset map with a\n * higher offset than what is found in the segment (i.e. messages with a key that appears in the dirty section of the log).\n * <p>\n * To avoid segments shrinking to very small sizes with repeated cleanings we implement a rule by which if we will merge successive segments when\n * doing a cleaning if their log and index size are less than the maximum log and index size prior to the clean beginning.\n * <p>\n * Cleaned segments are swapped into the log as they become available.\n * <p>\n * One nuance that the cleaner must handle is log truncation. If a log is truncated while it is being cleaned the cleaning of that log is aborted.\n * <p>\n * Messages with null payload are treated as deletes for the purpose of log compaction. This means that they receive special treatment by the cleaner.\n * The cleaner will only retain delete records for a period of time to avoid accumulating space indefinitely. This period of time is configurable on a per-topic\n * basis and is measured from the time the segment enters the clean portion of the log (at which point any prior message with that key has been removed).\n * Delete markers in the clean section of the log that are older than this time will not be retained when log segments are being recopied as part of cleaning.\n * This time is tracked by setting the base timestamp of a record batch with delete markers when the batch is recopied in the first cleaning that encounters\n * it. The relative timestamps of the records in the batch are also modified when recopied in this cleaning according to the new base timestamp of the batch.\n * <p>\n * Note that cleaning is more complicated with the idempotent/transactional producer capabilities. The following\n * are the key points:\n * <p>\n * <ol>\n * <li>In order to maintain sequence number continuity for active producers, we always retain the last batch\n *    from each producerId, even if all the records from the batch have been removed. The batch will be removed\n *    once the producer either writes a new batch or is expired due to inactivity.</li>\n * <li>We do not clean beyond the last stable offset. This ensures that all records observed by the cleaner have\n *    been decided (i.e. committed or aborted). In particular, this allows us to use the transaction index to\n *    collect the aborted transactions ahead of time.</li>\n * <li>Records from aborted transactions are removed by the cleaner immediately without regard to record keys.</li>\n * <li>Transaction markers are retained until all record batches from the same transaction have been removed and\n *    a sufficient amount of time has passed to reasonably ensure that an active consumer wouldn't consume any\n *    data from the transaction prior to reaching the offset of the marker. This follows the same logic used for\n *    tombstone deletion.</li>\n * </ol>\n */\npublic class LogCleaner implements BrokerReconfigurable {\n    private static final Logger LOG = LoggerFactory.getLogger(LogCleaner.class);\n","numLines":100,"startLine":1,"totalLines":655}}}

Segment selection is managed by LogCleanerManager.java (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleanerManager.java), which calculates which logs need cleaning based on a dirtiness ratio (the ratio of uncleanable bytes to total bytes). LogToClean.java (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogToClean.java) represents a log ready for cleaning and calculates the cleanableRatio metric that prioritizes which logs are dirtiest. The cleaner groups segments by size using groupSegmentsBySize() in Cleaner.java to prevent excessive segment fragmentation. For transactional support, CleanedTransactionMetadata.java manages aborted transaction state during cleaning, AbortedTxn.java represents aborted transactions, and TransactionIndex.java maintains indexes of aborted transactions. Configuration is centralized in CleanerConfig.java with parameters like deduplication buffer size, IO buffer size, and thread count. Cleaner.java contains critical methods: buildOffsetMap() and buildOffsetMapForSegment() construct a key=>offset mapping for the dirty section of the log, while shouldRetainRecord() implements the deduplication logic that retains only the latest record for each key. Segment selection is managed by LogCleanerManager.java (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleanerManager.java), which calculates which logs need cleaning based on a dirtiness ratio (the ratio of uncleanable bytes to total bytes). LogToClean.java (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogToClean.java) represents a log ready for cleaning and calculates the cleanableRatio metric that prioritizes which logs are dirtiest. The cleaner groups segments by size using groupSegmentsBySize() in Cleaner.java to prevent excessive segment fragmentation. For transactional support, CleanedTransactionMetadata.java manages aborted transaction state during cleaning, AbortedTxn.java represents aborted transactions, and TransactionIndex.java maintains indexes of aborted transactions. Configuration is centralized in CleanerConfig.java with parameters like deduplication buffer size, IO buffer size, and thread count. LogCleaningState.java defines the state machine for cleaning progress (InProgress, Aborted, Paused). Statistics are collected in CleanerStats.java and PreCleanStats.java to monitor cleaning performance and progress.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
